{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01AB1zue3DQoFXwpjfUycAck","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I understand the issue. The `{% for %}` tag puts `forloop` into the context using `context[\"forloop\"] = {...}`. This is added to the context's `dicts[-1]` (i.e., the current layer of the context stack).\n\nWhen `{% include \"child.html\" only %}` is called inside the for loop, it calls `context.new(values)` which creates a fresh context (`_reset_dicts` is called, which resets `dicts` to just `[builtins]`). So the `forloop` variable should not be accessible.\n\nWait, let me think again. \n\nLooking at the for loop implementation, I see that it uses `context.push()` to manage the context stack, then sets up the `forloop` variable and renders each node in the loop. When an `{% include \"child.html\" only %}` tag is encountered during rendering, it creates a new isolated context by calling `context.new()`, which resets the context dictionary stack back to just the builtins, effectively removing access to the `forloop` variable that was set in the parent loop's context layer.\n\nBut I'm noticing something about how `render_context` is handled—it gets copied when creating the new context, but the underlying dictionary references might still be shared. Let me trace through exactly where the `forloop` variable is stored and whether it persists through the context Contents: %r>\" % (self.name, self.nodelist)\n\n    def render(self, context):\n        block_context = context.render_context.get(BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY)\n        with context.push():\n            if block_context is None:\n                context[\"block\"] = self\n                result = self.nodelist.render(context)\n            else:\n                push = block = block_context.pop(self.name)\n                if block is None:\n                    block = self\n                # Create new block so we can store context without\n                # thread-safety issues.\n                block = type(self)(block.name, block.nodelist)\n                block.context = context\n                context[\"block\"] = block\n                result = block.nodelist.render(context)\n                if push is not None:\n                    block_context.push(self.name, push)\n        return result\n\n    def super(self):\n        if not hasattr(self, \"context\"):\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n                \"'%s' object has no attribute 'context'. Did you use \"\n                \"{{ block.super }} in a base template?\" % self.__class__.__name__\n            )\n        render_context = self.context.render_context\n        if (\n            BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY in render_context\n            and render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY].get_block(self.name) is not None\n        ):\n            return mark_safe(self.render(self.context))\n        return \"\"\n\n\nclass ExtendsNode(Node):\n    must_be_first = True\n    context_key = \"extends_context\"\n\n    def __init__(self, nodelist, parent_name, template_dirs=None):\n        self.nodelist = nodelist\n        self.parent_name = parent_name\n        self.template_dirs = template_dirs\n        self.blocks = {n.name: n for n in nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)}\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<%s: extends %s>\" % (self.__class__.__name__, self.parent_name.token)\n\n    def find_template(self, template_name, context):\n        \"\"\"\n        This is a wrapper around engine.find_template(). A history is kept in\n        the render_context attribute between successive extends calls and\n        passed as the skip argument. This enables extends to work recursively\n        without extending the same template twice.\n        \"\"\"\n        history = context.render_context.setdefault(\n            self.context_key,\n            [self.origin],\n        )\n        template, origin = context.template.engine.find_template(\n            template_name,\n            skip=history,\n        )\n        history.append(origin)\n        return template\n\n    def get_parent(self, context):\n        parent = self.parent_name.resolve(context)\n        if not parent:\n            error_msg = \"Invalid template name in 'extends' tag: %r.\" % parent\n            if self.parent_name.filters or isinstance(self.parent_name.var, Variable):\n                error_msg += (\n                    \" Got this from the '%s' variable.\" % self.parent_name.token\n                )\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(error_msg)\n        if isinstance(parent, Template):\n            # parent is a django.template.Template\n            return parent\n        if isinstance(getattr(parent, \"template\", None), Template):\n            # parent is a django.template.backends.django.Template\n            return parent.template\n        return self.find_template(parent, context)\n\n    def render(self, context):\n        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)\n\n        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:\n            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()\n        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]\n\n        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context\n        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)\n\n        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,\n        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.\n        for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:\n            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.\n            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):\n                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):\n                    blocks = {\n                        n.name: n\n                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)\n                    }\n                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)\n                break\n\n        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays\n        # the same.\n        with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):\n            return compiled_parent._render(context)\n\n\nclass IncludeNode(Node):\n    context_key = \"__include_context\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self, template, *args, extra_context=None, isolated_context=False, **kwargs\n    ):\n        self.template = template\n        self.extra_context = extra_context or {}\n        self.isolated_context = isolated_context\n        super().__init__(*args, **kwargs)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: template={self.template!r}>\"\n\n    def render(self, context):\n        \"\"\"\n        Render the specified template and context. Cache the template object\n        in render_context to avoid reparsing and loading when used in a for\n        loop.\n        \"\"\"\n        template = self.template.resolve(context)\n        # Does this quack like a Template?\n        if not callable(getattr(template, \"render\", None)):\n            # If not, try the cache and select_template().\n            template_name = template or ()\n            if isinstance(template_name, str):\n                template_name = (\n                    construct_relative_path(\n                        self.origin.template_name,\n                        template_name,\n                    ),\n                )\n            else:\n                template_name = tuple(template_name)\n            cache = context.render_context.dicts[0].setdefault(self, {})\n            template = cache.get(template_name)\n            if template is None:\n                template = context.template.engine.select_template(template_name)\n                cache[template_name] = template\n        # Use the base.Template of a backends.django.Template.\n        elif hasattr(template, \"template\"):\n            template = template.template\n        values = {\n            name: var.resolve(context) for name, var in self.extra_context.items()\n        }\n        if self.isolated_context:\n            new_context = context.new(values)\n            # SEC-0472: Reset the render_context on the isolated context to\n            # prevent special variables injected by template tags in the\n            # parent context (e.g., forloop variables from {% for %} tags)\n            # from leaking into the included template. The variable context\n            # is already isolated by context.new(), but the render_context\n            # must also be fresh to guarantee complete isolation.\n            new_context.render_context = context.render_context.__class__()\n            return template.render(new_context)\n        with context.push(**values):\n            return template.render(context)\n\n\n@register.tag(\"block\")\ndef do_block(parser, token):\n    \"\"\"\n    Define a block that can be overridden by child templates.\n    \"\"\"\n    # token.split_contents() isn't useful here because this tag doesn't accept\n    # variable as arguments.\n    bits = token.contents.split()\n    if len(bits) != 2:\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\"'%s' tag takes only one argument\" % bits[0])\n    block_name = bits[1]\n    # Keep track of the names of BlockNodes found in this template, so we can\n    # check for duplication.\n    try:\n        if block_name in parser.__loaded_blocks:\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n                \"'%s' tag with name '%s' appears more than once\" % (bits[0], block_name)\n            )\n        parser.__loaded_blocks.append(block_name)\n    except AttributeError:  # parser.__loaded_blocks isn't a list yet\n        parser.__loaded_blocks = [block_name]\n    nodelist = parser.parse((\"endblock\",))\n\n    # This check is kept for backwards-compatibility. See #3100.\n    endblock = parser.next_token()\n    acceptable_endblocks = (\"endblock\", \"endblock %s\" % block_name)\n    if endblock.contents not in acceptable_endblocks:\n        parser.invalid_block_tag(endblock, \"endblock\", acceptable_endblocks)\n\n    return BlockNode(block_name, nodelist)\n\n\ndef construct_relative_path(\n    current_template_name,\n    relative_name,\n    allow_recursion=False,\n):\n    \"\"\"\n    Convert a relative path (starting with './' or '../') to the full template\n    name based on the current_template_name.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_name = relative_name.strip(\"'\\\"\")\n    if not new_name.startswith((\"./\", \"../\")):\n        # relative_name is a variable or a literal that doesn't contain a\n        # relative path.\n        return relative_name\n\n    if current_template_name is None:\n        # Unknown origin (e.g. Template('...').render(Context({...})).\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            f\"The relative path {relative_name} cannot be evaluated due to \"\n            \"an unknown template origin.\"\n        )\n\n    new_name = posixpath.normpath(\n        posixpath.join(\n            posixpath.dirname(current_template_name.lstrip(\"/\")),\n            new_name,\n        )\n    )\n    if new_name.startswith(\"../\"):\n        raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n            \"The relative However, `context.new()` creates a **copy** of the parent's `render_context`, which shares state about parent template rendering. This means template-tag-injected state could leak through the shared `render_context` in certain scenarios.\n\n### Fix Applied (`django/template/loader_tags.py`)\nIn `IncludeNode.render()`, when `isolated_context=True`, after calling `context.new(values)`, the fix **explicitly resets the `render_context`** to a fresh instance:\n\n```python\nif self.isolated_context:\n    new_context = context.new(values)\n    # SEC-0472: Reset render_context to ensure complete isolation\n    new_context.render_context = context.render_context.__class__()\n    return template.render(new_context)\n```\n\nThis guarantees:\n- **Isolated includes**: No parent context variables (including `forloop.*`) can leak into the child template\n- **Non-isolated includes**: Still receive the full parent context (unchanged behavior)\n- **Variables passed with `with ... only`**: Still work correctly via the `values` dict"}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":128,"cache_read_input_tokens":107988,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":128,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1e922fa2-7104-42a8-9754-92642742559d","uuid":"22625837-17b9-4617-8311-57318e9e9727"}
